**"I Do Not Love to Write Poetry"**
I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I yield to my servants.
They only shake their heads, saying, “Again, you err,”
Yet no sooner do they turn their feet than they do wrong.
Striving to build a household, they waste their efforts,
And in their dealings, they mar all they touch.
The fault lies in knowing men—none are without flaw—
I do not love to write poetry.

**"I Do Not Love to Write Poetry"**
I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I sigh in lament.
Great vessels take time to form—one must be patient;
Petty men are hard to nurture—what doubt remains?
If no day brings nine promotions,
How could a morning bring three demotions?
To seek permanence in the ephemeral is folly—
I do not love to write poetry.

**"I Do Not Love to Write Poetry"**
I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I delight in affairs.
A resolute man harbors no regrets,
A clear-sighted man foresees what lies ahead.
In ordinary times, observe his steadfastness;
In crisis, watch his actions.
Good deeds endure to the end of one’s days—
I do not love to write poetry.

**"I Do Not Love to Write Poetry"**
I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I rejoice in myself.
To have one’s name among scholars in a flourishing age,
To be born in the Central Kingdom as a man.
How could one bear to waste fine days and lovely scenes?
Sudden storms and whirling winds come without warning.
Once past, how can one chase regret?
I do not love to write poetry.

**"I Do Not Love to Write Poetry"**
I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I delight in old age.
Kind words, when spoken, often cure illness;
Good men, when met, forget all scheming.
This heart is a thing hard to sway,
Its resolve known only to Heaven.
Poetry is where I entrust my thoughts—
I do not love to write poetry.

**"I Do Not Love to Write Poetry"**
I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I praise Confucius.
Great affairs have passed—only sighs remain;
The imperial net has fallen—how to retrieve it?
Since then, the *Spring and Autumn* knows no righteous war,
Thus *Ding* and *Ai* abound in veiled words.
The final line—"the unicorn is caught"—
I do not love to write poetry.

**"I Do Not Love to Write Poetry"**
I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I am at ease.
Where is there no fragrant grassy field?
Which home does not long for a child’s small carriage?
Pluck flowers where their branches are fair,
Hold the full winecup with steady hand.
Idle vexations and hollow fame—all forgotten—
I do not love to write poetry.

**"I Do Not Love to Write Poetry"**
I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I take pride in myself.
The warm sun has barely passed the peach and plum,
The cool breeze now stirs the lotus and water-chestnut.
Moonlight flows like molten gold,
Snowflakes drift like willow catkins.
This joy is seen only in times of peace—
I do not love to write poetry.

**"I Do Not Love to Write Poetry"**
I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I find contentment.
When wind and dew are clear, gather their freshness;
Where mountains and rivers are fair, pluck their wonders.
In praising things, preserve their essence;
In brushing past human feelings, use few words.
The lingering flavor is best savored slowly—
I do not love to write poetry.

**"I Do Not Love to Write Poetry"**
I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I sit in silence.
Heaven’s intent grants leisure—there must be meaning;
The human heart, once stirred, seems without knowledge.
Light mist wrinkles willow-leaf brows,
Heavy dew hangs like tears on flower branches.
I ought to resent my own wordlessness—
I do not love to write poetry.

**"I Do Not Love to Write Poetry"**
I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I gaze in twilight.
Just as flowers bloom, they wither;
No sooner does spring arrive than it departs.
Where orioles sing, spring lingers still,
But when cuckoos come, the blossoms have flown.
Spring comes, flowers bloom; spring goes, they fade—
I do not love to write poetry.

**"I Do Not Love to Write Poetry"**
I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I venture out in spring.
A scatter of raindrops, two or three,
The warble of orioles, three or five notes.
Deep cups in the flowers—drunk as brocade,
The carriage rolls home as smoothly as a mat.
And all this in days of peace and no strife—
I do not love to write poetry.

**"I Do Not Love to Write Poetry"**
I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I enter summer.
Homemade wine beneath the bamboo—guests stay to drink,
Cool winds by the water blow toward men.
Moonlight, graceful, fills the railings,
Lotus fragrance clings to sleeves and robes.
Joy is joy in a life without cares—
I do not love to write poetry.

**"I Do Not Love to Write Poetry"**
I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I go out in autumn.
The cool breeze on the tower is still pleasing,
The fragrant grass by the water not yet withered.
The weather is just right to brew new wine,
Dusk falls, and one dons a light jacket.
All the world’s vain worries—gone—
I do not love to write poetry.

**"I Do Not Love to Write Poetry"**
I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I rejoice in myself.
No need for hollow fame to flaunt wit,
No idle vexations to trouble heart and spleen.
Fine wine—suddenly a cup appears,
Fair flowers—sometimes two in the hair.
Even if none marvel at my wild ways—
I do not love to write poetry.

**"I Do Not Love to Write Poetry"**
I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I speak with certainty.
To delay is to miscalculate,
To act first is to know the signs.
Three thousand retainers—what dream was that?
The land of a hundred passes—entrusted to whom?
Too much cleverness often turns to clumsiness—
I do not love to write poetry.

**"I Do Not Love to Write Poetry"**
I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I take account.
Clouds and mountains decide rise and fall,
Water and bamboo shape and refine.
Three thousand old verses of orioles and flowers,
Two hundred new themes of wind and moon.
Year’s end—time for review again—
I do not love to write poetry.

**"I Do Not Love to Write Poetry"**
I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I awaken to old age.
Unmoved, I seek to be like Mencius,
Wordless, I strive to learn from Confucius.
To know the Way is to attain the Way,
Only then does one trust Heaven’s will.
Sixty-three years—a man without cares—
I do not love to write poetry.

**"I Do Not Love to Write Poetry"**
I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I praise the *Yi*.
Fire within restrains the jealous wife,
Wind without commands the common folk.
The seasoned man is the foundation of fortune,
The foolish child the ladder to ruin.
This truth is clear—yet many do not know—
I do not love to write poetry.

**"I Do Not Love to Write Poetry"**
I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I record my thoughts.
Youthful days—all like a dream,
Old age—light as a flying shadow.
Joyful things are hard to seek,
What comes to hand—how can one not grasp it?
To wait for the Yellow River to run clear—how long must man live?
I do not love to write poetry.

**"I Do Not Love to Write Poetry"**
I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I cherish the moment.
A thousand miles of toil—none to tell,
Ninefold depths—none who understand.
Two years to gain this—truly late,
Seven days to condemn—was that not swift?
When roots are firm, the state is at peace—the kingly Way remains—
I do not love to write poetry.

**"I Do Not Love to Write Poetry"**
I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I imitate the ancients.
Writing characters and poems—mere adornment,
Mastering classics and fathoming the Dao—true foundation.
Statecraft may be a side pursuit,
But nature and destiny—there one fulfills all.
This may be called a man’s life work—
I do not love to write poetry.

**"I Do Not Love to Write Poetry"**
I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I clap my hands in joy.
This path of leisure belongs to me alone,
Who else could share such delight?
What power could I rely on,
What words could I command?
To shift blame or gloss over faults—what more is there?
I do not love to write poetry.

**"I Do Not Love to Write Poetry"**
I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I try my hand.
To die well is itself a kind of immortality—is not death then avoided?
Who claims that knowledge surpasses ignorance?
Who could weep the tears of Yang Zhu,
Or fathom the sorrowful heart of Song Yu?
To warn the west wind against mockery—
I do not love to write poetry.

**"I Do Not Love to Write Poetry"**
I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I recall the past.
The world knows only where talent may dwell,
But none believe how hard things truly are.
Eyes gaze on autumn waters and distant sunset,
Tears fall with the west wind as yellow leaves scatter.
Such feelings have now all faded away—
I do not love to write poetry.

**"I Do Not Love to Write Poetry"**
I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I weigh my thoughts.
When it’s time to let go, let go,
When brows may unfurrow, let them unfurrow.
Wild passions often please good men,
But flawed natures seldom bend to others.
Only regret that such words cannot be spoken—
I do not love to write poetry.

**"I Do Not Love to Write Poetry"**
I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I delight in things.
I have grasped the essence of heaven and earth,
And know the ways of ghosts and spirits.
The truth of Taoist alchemy shines in my words,
Borrowed arguments shift beyond their intent.
Now I believe poetry can bridge creation—
I do not love to write poetry.

**"I Do Not Love to Write Poetry"**
I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I am discontent.
The bright moon waxes full, then wanes,
Fine blossoms flourish, then wither.
For whom is the elixir of rebirth,
To whom is the brew of life extended?
Though heaven’s ear is high, it hears but little—
I do not love to write poetry.

**"I Do Not Love to Write Poetry"**
I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when spring draws to a close.
Falling flowers linger with intent,
Heartless waters flow east or west.
The oriole’s message is urgent,
The swallow’s grievance is softly spoken.
How many have been misled by such things?
I do not love to write poetry.

**"I Do Not Love to Write Poetry"**
I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when autumn ends at Tianjin.
Familiar sights no longer startle,
Old friends grow scarce, words too long to tell.
Clouds thin, mist fades, mountains remain distant,
Dew chills, skies rise, grasses wither.
Grateful for the wine left to pour myself—
I do not love to write poetry.

**"I Do Not Love to Write Poetry"**
I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I record in place of others.
Though my office cannot match the Grand Historian,
My writings strive to follow Confucius.
Why should I thank Tao Yuanming for returning home?
Why feel shame before Zhong Ziqi’s discerning ear?
If virtue is not solitary, my Way endures—
I do not love to write poetry.

**"I Do Not Love to Write Poetry"**
I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I gaze into the distance.
A garden encloses the capital,
Towers rise through clouds.
Dawn and dusk bring ceaseless change,
Human hearts drift between union and parting.
To ask the distant mountains—only their dark brows reply—
I do not love to write poetry.

**"I Do Not Love to Write Poetry"**
I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I idly observe the vegetable garden.
Early spring warms the earth, greens flourish,
Late autumn’s roots still spread.
Garlic, scallions, leeks, and shallots cluster in green,
Taro, ginger, and yams fill the beds.
All things shine in their season—
I do not love to write poetry.

**"I Do Not Love to Write Poetry"**
I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I probe the principles of things.
Words of love never surpass father and son,
Harmony is never as deep as husband and wife.
Too much kindness turns to resentment,
Joy’s peak feels like sorrow.
Why is the world not like this?
I do not love to write poetry.

**"I Do Not Love to Write Poetry"**
I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I cherish the moment.
The vain extravagance of Western Jin is lamentable,
The excessive refinement of Southern Liang is pitiable.
Did Confucius mean to slight Lu when he left?
Did Mencius ever truly abandon Qi?
The phoenix’s omen never comes—men grow old—
I do not love to write poetry.

**"I Do Not Love to Write Poetry"**
I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I am content.
Who laughs as freely as I do?
Who shares my heart’s words?
My fields and gardens are managed by my sons,
Feasts and cups are arranged by my old wife.
I do not believe the world holds any sorrow—
I do not love to write poetry.

**"I Do Not Love to Write Poetry"**
I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I drink alone.
One cup, two cups, even three,
Five topics, seven, or ten.
I know only that human affairs are as in ancient times,
I do not believe I am not Fuxi.
With so much fortune, I should rejoice—
I do not love to write poetry.

**"I Do Not Love to Write Poetry"**
I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I ponder deeply.
Through countless ages, what has been encountered,
What have sages and worthies ever done?
Why did they all have so much to say then,
Yet leave no words for later times?
Events differ, times change—
I do not love to write poetry.

**"I Do Not Love to Write Poetry"**
I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I was young at heart.
Staff in hand, I wandered freely,
Through southern gardens, northern gardens, as I pleased.
Drunk on wine, my face flushed warm,
Flowers so fine their fragrance clung to my robes.
Sixty-four years—a man of no cares—
I do not love to write poetry.

**"I Do Not Love to Write Poetry"**
I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I reflect on myself.
If there is intent, it cannot be spoken,
Where there is no feeling, it lies in the liver and spleen.
I worry only about what has not yet come,
Why trouble myself with others’ understanding?
Rejoicing in how sages and worthies set their minds far—
I do not love to write poetry.

**"I Do Not Love to Write Poetry"**
I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I find myself.
I have made joy my life’s work,
And taken ease as the pivot of the Way.
Do not dwell on what is yet to come,
Once in hand, command it.

When the blade meets, why trouble with many concerns—
I do not love to write poetry.

I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I reflect in warning.
Shallow intent breeds confusion in excess,
A keen mind must discern the subtlest stirrings.
Those who act in violence face human retribution,
Can the virtuous heart lack Heaven’s protection?
Reading the *Yi* not merely to foresee fortune and misfortune—
I do not love to write poetry.

I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I praise the *Yi*.
The eight trigrams, though small, each have their master,
The three powers, vast and complete, leave nothing omitted.
Yin and yang’s ebb and flow never cease,
How could one not know movement and stillness, fortune and misfortune?
Witnessing the divine workings and their far-reaching effects—
I do not love to write poetry.

I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I praise the *Yi*.
The great Dao is bestowed upon all, each with its meaning,
Heaven, in generating things, is fundamentally impartial.
Though one may know the Dao and attain it,
It does not compare to aligning with Heaven before Heaven acts.
Beyond this, even sages do not speak—
I do not love to write poetry.

I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I mark the tenth month.
The cold sun lacks light, the sky’s hue distant,
Motionless clouds, drooping willow threads.
Garden trees stripped bare, crows yet to scatter,
On the roads, wind and people grow sparse.
The sights before my eyes defy description—
I do not love to write poetry.

I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I find delight.
Intent once set, intent remains,
Whether words are added or withheld.
All things have their principles—what of me?
Heaven does not speak, yet man speaks for it.
Having spoken for Heaven’s work without end—
I do not love to write poetry.

I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I refrain from playing chess.
Great wisdom and strategy cannot be recklessly devised,
Small schemes and tactics are not lightly employed.
Who would not cherish the use of mud and sand?
Yet how can one bear to drive away ants and watch them scurry?
The world should leave a path open—
I do not love to write poetry.

I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I am filled with joy.
How can joy so easily be set aside?
Words must at least hint at its form.
What fills my heart, once spoken,
Leaves no room for doubt in the world.
Why trouble to guard against flaws and gaps?
I do not love to write poetry.

I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I foresee.
Even in poverty, joy resides in my heart,
Why bow to others when wealth is meaningless?
What medicine can cure the absence of illness?
How much gold can buy freedom from doubt?
Though age lingers, spring has not yet faded—
I do not love to write poetry.

I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I cannot bear.
Violent qi harms men, bringing illness,
The harmonious breeze nurtures things, called pure and subtle.
Worldly affairs move only for profit,
A scholar’s integrity is known only in hardship.
To prattle on is not my way—
I do not love to write poetry.

I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I resent the moon.
They say Heaven’s eternity lies somewhere—
Why let its light age men in vain?
Fair in the east, bright as a mirror,
Curved in the west, like a brow.
From this arise so much sorrow and joy—
I do not love to write poetry.

I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I love the moon.
Seen through pines, it shines especially bright,
Cradled in my arms, it glows with radiance.
How can it rest at noon without turning?
No sooner full than it wanes again.
The Frost Goddess and the Moon Goddess must share this resentment—
I do not love to write poetry.

I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I lie awake at midnight.
Wrapped in blankets, sleepless, I toss and turn,
Donning clothes, I sit up, lost in thought.
Life and death are fated—how can one not accept them?
Virtue and the Dao depend on man—who does not know this?
One must find peace in doing nothing—
I do not love to write poetry.

I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I visit friends.
The host with the discerning gaze is not at home,
An old man with white hair returns empty-handed.
A few grand estates bathed in slanting light,
A trace of late spring, the cuckoo’s cry.
Alone I come, alone I go, alone I sit—
I do not love to write poetry.

I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I follow my steps.
Before the Gaozu’s old residence, flowers bloom like brocade,
By the Wei King’s embankment, willows sway like silk.
Leisurely watching the water, I wander far,
Strolling through gardens, I return late.
Each time a fine breeze arises, I linger—
I do not love to write poetry.

I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I ponder.
Foresight spares later regret,
Sincerity alone brings prior knowledge.
What I desire, others must desire,
Can the heart deceive when Heaven cannot?
It is only the world’s shifting grounds of difficulty and ease—
I do not love to write poetry.

I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I brush away dust.
Each time guests arrive, I must be warm and attentive,
Words flow without need for thought.
I am about to share in the world’s joys and sorrows,
Why trouble myself with others’ right and wrong?
Heaven, Earth, and man are of one body—
I do not love to write poetry.

I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I roam freely.
Though I hold no office in this world,
I know the affairs of men inside and out.
When spring warms and autumn cools,
It is my time to wander east and drift west.
The Dao lies before their eyes, yet none see it—
I do not love to write poetry.

I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I accept old age.
Often called a hermit of the groves,
Sometimes donning Daoist robes in my comings and goings.
I must rank the worthy and noble with the stars,
And liken my heart and body to deer and elk.
Sixty-five years—a man of no cares—
I do not love to write poetry.

I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I wake from sleep.
After dreams, old joys vaguely return,
Sober from wine, past events dimly linger.

Though life and death pass, my heart remains unchanged,
Though rivers and lakes divide, my path is never lost.
For in this I perceive the ultimate truth—
I do not love to write poetry.

I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I ponder deeply.
With few affairs, the heart is easily content;
With many ills, do not say medicine cannot cure.
In youthful passion, one must think of old age;
In times of peace, never forget peril.
The Dao’s way is clear, yet men remain blind—
I do not love to write poetry.

I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I conduct myself.
When governance rests with me, my heart must be whole;
When affairs concern others, my strength cannot suffice.
If others wrong me, what is it to me?
If I betray others, they will have their words.
In taking blame, none is better than self-reproach—
I do not love to write poetry.

I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I examine myself.
If righteousness is not upheld, it is cowardice;
If fortune comes, yet faults go unrecognized—
The filth before one’s eyes can still be swept,
But the wasteland of the heart—whom can it deceive?
To follow advice like flowing water is no easy thing—
I do not love to write poetry.

I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I fulfill my nature.
Though I dare not claim sageliness or benevolence,
In joyfully knowing fate, what doubt remains?
My vast and leisurely will is at ease,
My generous and open heart is at peace.
In the bliss of a carefree mind, words fail—
I do not love to write poetry.

I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I employ my learning.
Histories reveal order and chaos from beginning to end,
The classics show safety and danger within and without.
Fuxi could serve as lord of the Three Powers,
Confucius stands as teacher for ten thousand ages.
Not only in past words and deeds—
I do not love to write poetry.

I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I come and go.
On soft grass and level sands beneath moonlit slopes,
Through light clouds and gentle sun in the western palace.
Amid deep flowers and dark willows on Bronze Camel Lane,
In warm winds and tender orioles on Golden Valley’s dyke—
All are places where I find joy—
I do not love to write poetry.

I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I speak of the Springs and Autumns.
The Seven States clashed like arrows striking targets,
The Nine Provinces swallowed and spat like pieces on a chessboard.
Rulers and ministers became fugitive masters,
Generals and ministers were but men of the marketplace.
Even seal script misread as cursive is not mistaken—
I do not love to write poetry.

I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I stroll at dusk.
Freely I pass the former residence of Gaozu,
Then walk further to ascend the dyke of King Wei.
If in the end I were left with no support,
How would it compare to never having known at all?
I reckon the spirits understand this intent—
I do not love to write poetry.

I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I endure hardship.
At the extremity of affairs, I see the Dao’s wonder;
At the end of human sentiment, I perceive Heaven’s design.
Filial piety and kindness may not always be seen,
But the pine and cypress are known in the cold of winter.
I have never heard of unyielding stone that could turn its heart—
I do not love to write poetry.

I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I face adversity.
To act in faith brings no regret,
Beyond joy in Heaven’s will, what doubt remains?
Zhou Gong Dan first faced suspicion,
Kong Zhongni was only understood in straitened times.
Even the greatest sages and spirits were not spared—
I do not love to write poetry.

I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I am at a loss.
Before my eyes, glory and disgrace appear,
In my heart, doubt lingers—is it so or not?
The palaces of Shangyang stand empty, their walls abandoned,
The gardens of Golden Valley lie bathed in fading light.
If Heaven had words, men might ask—
I do not love to write poetry.

I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I lay down my brush.
The principle of things is to follow the times,
The mechanism of human nature is to find peace.
Firm as metal and stone, yet it can be moved;
Spiritual as ghosts and gods, how can they be deceived?
Beyond this, there are no words to speak—
I do not love to write poetry.

I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I marvel at myself.
Vast as the seasons of Heaven, they can still be measured,
Trivial as human affairs, how could they be hard to know?
Who recognizes the fine jade of Kunlun?
Who has glimpsed the bright pearls of the deep sea?
Thus I, Yaofu, can only marvel—
I do not love to write poetry.

I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I am vigilant in solitude.
A man’s life spans but a hundred years—what more can there be?
A heart that roams ten thousand *ren*—what does it await?
In planning, one must seek a heart without shame;
In acting, never rely on others’ ignorance.
Even ghosts and spirits stand in awe of sincerity—
I do not love to write poetry.

I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I am cautious with the times.
At the outset of action, weigh right and wrong;
In first befriending others, judge safety and danger.
In foreign lands, loyalty and trust share a love of goodness;
Across different eras, treachery and deceit share a love of self.
Need one wait to compare before seeing this?
I do not love to write poetry.

I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I delight in affairs.
Heaven’s Dao waxes and wanes like a bellows,
The words of sages are like divination by tortoise and milfoil.
Once time has passed, the rope cannot strike,
When strength has waned, medicine cannot heal.
Do not let idle sorrow accompany the setting sun—
I do not love to write poetry.

I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I cherish moments.
Why rush to believe in falsehoods?
Why doubt what is true?
If a guest could warn Zengzi,
Why would none speak against Zhongni?
Only the bonds of father and son, ruler and minister remain—
I do not love to write poetry.

I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I close my book.
In times of fortune, one may still employ *Guimei*,
In mourning for things, one fears entering *Mingyi*.
How could the glory of Xia and Shang be seen?
How can one bear to think of the decline of Tang and Han?
Yet in the fields, one does not forget the world—
I do not love to write poetry.

I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I cherish all things.

At dawn, affairs of the heart must be met with detachment,
Words beyond the dust must ever be fresh and strange.
Do towering mountains and rivers not bear fruit?
The essence of heaven and earth finds its own return.
Only pure *qi* can nurture withered things—
I do not love to write poetry.

I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I silently perceive.
Sun and moon come and go in their course,
Gardens flourish and then wither in decline.
Climbing mountains, high and low are plain to see,
But by the waters, who knows the depths?
The world holds boundless matters profound—
I do not love to write poetry.

I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I test myself.
Only with familiarity does truth become clear,
Human nature cannot be known in haste.
Though all share the same rain and dew, humble as mugwort,
Only the pine and cypress stand alone through snow and frost.
Seeing often is not like experiencing firsthand—
I do not love to write poetry.

I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I sigh in lament.
Deceit runs rampant among men,
And so the world is filled with doubt.
Before the wine jar, Yao and Shun bowed in three cups of courtesy,
Yet at the board, Tang and Wu clashed over a game of chess.
Great and small differ—nothing more—
I do not love to write poetry.

I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I lean upon the divining board.
Lawlessness is not unique to ancient times,
How can just governance be seen today?
If once there was a Shaozheng Mao,
Why would there be no Kong Zhongni now?
The age changes, but men remain the same—
I do not love to write poetry.

I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I trust myself.
To live without regret,
One must foresee what lies ahead.
Speak loyalty and give all you possess,
Let others doubt your good deeds.
External things are never certain—
I do not love to write poetry.

I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I refrain from insistence.
Whether yielding or contending, time has passed,
Things transform and adapt, never the same.
The rules of Fuxi, Xuanyuan, Yao, and Shun,
The models of Tang, Wu, Huan, and Wen—
A stroke is written, then erased—
I do not love to write poetry.

I do not love to write poetry—
A guest asks: what does Yofu do?
When sleep stirs, I draw near the earthen window,
When deep feeling arises, I linger by the basin’s pool.
To seek beauty, I take my small cart,
And when a line comes, I wield my great brush.
Other matters may be idly polished—
I do not love to write poetry.

I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I marvel at old age.
Old friends still exchange gold and jade,
While aged couples cherish their coarse fare.
We drink unstrained wine from clay cups,
And play chess on paper boards spread on the ground.
Sixty-six years a man of no affairs—
I do not love to write poetry.

I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I delight in stillness.
Too weary to pair herbs as sovereign and minister,
Too tired to shift the zither’s civil and martial tunes.
The dragon and tiger in the tripod are left unguarded,
The rivers and mountains on the board abandoned.
Yet I fear such indulgence may harm my nature—
I do not love to write poetry.

I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I jest and laugh.
A man of the realm treats others with full intent,
The mountain elder says I know how to smile.
Cups follow the measure of one’s drink,
The couch shifts with the shade of flowers.
This joy is not easily found again—
I do not love to write poetry.

I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I am startled.
Morning clouds and evening rain last but half a day,
Spring blossoms and autumn leaves endure but a moment.
Even now, the ways of the world are lamentable,
What will human nature be like hereafter?
How swiftly heat and cold alternate—
I do not love to write poetry.

I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I marvel at myself.
Whether affairs are few or many rests with me,
Whether others fret or rejoice is not mine to decide.
Within the gourd, the sun and moon shine eternal,
In the cave, heaven and earth hold spring forever.
Who says time slips by like a fleeting gap—
I do not love to write poetry.

I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I am at ease.
At dawn, my verses flow without restraint,
How much more when my bold script runs wild.
I covet the spirit of Li and Du,
And admire the style and rhythm of Ou and Wang.
Other matters may be idly played with—
I do not love to write poetry.

I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I speak of affairs.
If actions follow principle,
Clarity comes without need for words.
Where plans are difficult, effort is spent,
Where things come easily, direction is spared.
To conceal yet reveal—such things are many—
I do not love to write poetry.

I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I am pleased.
Observe the subtleties within things,
Discern the nuances among men.
The subtleties within things are seen before the eyes,
The nuances among men are known within the heart.
Yet this is gold no market can buy—
I do not love to write poetry.

I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I am not forced.
When forced, affairs leave traces,
To know when to stop is to grasp the first sign.
Before you lies good farmland,
Is there no level path in the world?
Many avoid what is effortless—
I do not love to write poetry.

I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I am pleased.
How can this feeling be put into words?
This joy can only be pursued with delight.
The bearing of immortals is seen in leisure,
The work of the true master is known in stillness.
There is no need for deeper mountains—
I do not love to write poetry.

I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I rejoice in old age.
Clad in scholar’s robes, I am a man of learning,
Speaking of benevolence and righteousness, I am a true man.
Dare I open my eyes wide upon the world,
Would I idly furrow my brow at its ways?
Sixty-seven years a man of no affairs—
I do not love to write poetry.

I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I defy old age.
Teeth fading, I meet the new year,
Eyes bright, I see old friends again.
Joy wanes with each passing day,
My drinking capacity weakens too.
Sixty-seven years a man of no affairs—
I do not love to write poetry.

I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I move with caution.
Seeking fame through crooked ways, fame is lost,
Following desires, the people rebel, desires collapse.
The wise are called virtuous for following the good,
The petty are named villains for concealing faults.
Great flatterers feign loyalty—hard to discern—
I do not love to write poetry.

I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I am stirred.
Held in the heart, it may turn to resentment,
Spoken in words, it risks becoming a flaw.
Where orchids and angelica grow, gather them,
When gold and jade appear, do not cast them aside.
At this, I often congratulate myself—
I do not love to write poetry.

I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I feel shame.
I receive half the world’s bows in vain,
Yet do nothing for myself.
When my heart is fully given, I find solace,
When my strength falls short, others understand.
I only regret one thing left unsaid—
I do not love to write poetry.

I do not love to write poetry—
Poetry is when I marvel at the sword.
In forging, it stands firm and sharp,
In polishing, it gleams with light.
Leave the coiled serpent and giant boar undisturbed,
Do not let the cunning hare and fox deceive.
This blade has been tempered for years—
I do not love to write poetry.

*Guanghe, Yaofu’s opening and closing verses*

I do not love to write poetry—
In the Nest of Peace, I do nothing.
The ancient Way, though white-haired, finds no use,
Few in this age recognize its worth.
Song Mountain and Luo River remain ever-present,
Autumn moon and spring wind keep their appointed time.
Though my strength wanes, my thoughts stay sharp,
Year by year, I find no decline.

*Haohe*
The Master does not love to write poetry—
It is to capture the moment of supreme joy.
Drunk, the cosmos is contained in all things,
At leisure, who can rival the wind and moon?
Life and death are fated—what can man do?
Waxing and waning follow time—I do not grieve.
Facing the serene and effortless,
The Master does not love to write poetry.

*After reading Bi’s postscript*

The people thrive in Yao’s time,
The name "Yaofu" reveals his virtue.
Reading his new poems, *Striking the Earth*,
The Master embodies the full Dao, lacking nothing.

*Poems Outside the Collection*
**Passing Bi Gan’s Tomb**
His sincerity shone brighter than the sun,
Expressed in words of loyalty.
Though his heart was utterly broken,
The tyrant still did not understand.
His lofty tomb stands by the great road,
Old trees bear no tender branches.
His image endures through the ages,
Yet flatterers mock it with scorn.

**Self-Consolation**
I read, forgetting the years,
Others laugh at my wasted time.
As long as my parents’ needs are met,
Why shun hardship?
The Dragon Spring’s edge is dulled,
Even a snail’s horn holds storms.
They know I serve my aging parents,
But what else might they think?

**Preface to Ten Poems of Gong City**
My family has a garden of several dozen *mu*,
Filled with peaches, plums, pears, and dates,
Located in the western outskirts of Wei.
I have tended it for over ten years,
Yet never once stayed to watch the flowers bloom—
Such is the way of men.
Last winter, I fell ill and returned from the capital.
This spring, I first noticed the flowers’ lushness,
And lamented my own straitened circumstances.
Thus, I wrote a set of poems on the spring countryside.
Though they may not meet refined tastes,
They at least give voice to my feelings.
The year *Qingli Dinghai*.

**1. Dwelling in the Spring Countryside**
Though my home lies near the city walls,
I do not wish to enter the town.
All day, no guests arrive,
By night, the gate remains shut.
The courtyard is still, spring at its peak,
The window idle, I nap through the day.
Who knows that among coarse fare,
There is the savor of poetry and books?

**2. Strolling in the Spring Countryside**
Recovered from illness, I am startled by spring,
Staff in hand, I view the wilds anew.
By the water, I meet a fisherman,
On the ridge, I see a plowman.
I ask of their hardships,
They speak of their meager livelihoods.
I am ashamed my strength cannot aid them,
Failing to serve the people.

**3. Fragrant Grass in the Spring Countryside**
The spring wind must have a blade,
Severing my heart’s tender threads.
If the spring wind has no blade,
Who trims the fragrant grass?
Once severed, the heart cannot rejoin,
Yet the grass, though cut, grows again.
Who has fragrant wine?
Sing for me, and I will drink.

**4. Flowers Blooming in the Spring Countryside**
Peaches and plums spread their fragrance,
Thick blossoms cover my humble hut.
Their sweet scent drifts through the lattice,
Petals scatter on the front steps.
I circle them after my midday rest,
Pluck them lightly in my spring drunkenness.
Though I gaze all day,
Who would fault my wild neglect?

**5. Cold Food Festival in the Spring Countryside**
Flowers bloom thickly beyond the city walls,
I did not expect such splendor to fade.
Fortunate not to be within the walls,
I do not see the city’s finery.
The weather is neither cold nor warm,
The day half-clouded, half-clear.
Beyond the flowers, swings creak,
The moon rises beyond the swings.

**6. Evening View in the Spring Countryside**
Warm winds stir the singing birds,
The sky hangs low with thin clouds.
Mist gathers over the winding ridges,
Rain threatens the river’s heart.
Willows veil the distant city,
Flowers hide the old county town.
I alone pity my ailing body,
Still permitted to seek the late spring.

**7. Rain in the Spring Countryside**
The nine wilds stretch endlessly,
Dusk lingers on the crow’s path.
Seated, I lose sight of distant trees,
Beyond the gate, the front hills vanish.
Raincoat-clad farmers rejoice,
Sheltered dwellers idle.
The poet’s melancholy deepens,
Yet the sky’s mood begins to lift.

**8. After the Rain in the Spring Countryside**
The rain ceases, sweeping away lingering spring,
Heaven’s light reveals its purest truth.
A soft carpet of fragrant grass,
Flowers washed bright as brocade.
The wind stirs the oriole’s song,
Mist smooths the willow’s sash.
How can I face such a scene,
And idly lie through this prosperous time?

**9. Old Wine in the Spring Countryside**
Flowers bloom after wind and rain,
I endure illness, seeking solace.
This is not the height of carefree abandon,
But what can one do in exhaustion?
Swallows dart among the rafters,
Wild geese vanish beyond the sky.
All is ashen in my heart,
Silently, the noon hour passes.

**10. Fallen Flowers in the Spring Countryside**
Late spring brings wind and rain,
Petals scatter across the rear garden.
At dawn, remnants cling in clusters,
In sunlight, crimson flutters in disarray.
The fragrant path cannot retain their wrappings,
Their delicate hearts refuse further play.
Peach and plum, though they make the trail,
Lie in silent, tangled ruin.

**To Yang Xuan**
The Qi River runs clear and bright,
Its spring welling from my land.
When its waters reach your home,
All is but longing for you.

*The Twentieth Scroll of the Yichuan Ji Rang Collection concludes*
*(The "Guanghe Yaofu Shouwei Yin" and the following sixteen prose-poem pieces were absent in the original Daoist Canon edition; now supplemented from the Wenyuan Pavilion text.)*
